Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Effect of Qadi's Judgment in Agency to Return a Defective Slave-Girl
Intra-Hanafi dispute on effect of qadi's judgment in agency for return of defective property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn vs. Abu Yusuf's preferred view) on the revocability of a qadi's judgment in cases of agency to return a defective slave-girl, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
A qadi's judgment may be final or reversible depending on whether it is effective externally only or both externally and internally.

This passage from Kitab al-Wakalah in al-Hidayah explores a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school. When a buyer's agent attempts to return a defective slave-girl, and the seller claims the buyer was satisfied, the question arises: can the agent return her without the buyer's oath? The answer depends on whether the qadi's judgment to annul the sale is effective both outwardly and inwardly (zahiran wa batina) or only outwardly. Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on this foundational principle, leading to divergent rulings. Additionally, a preferred view from Abu Yusuf introduces a third option based on consideration for the parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Understand that the case is about an agent appointed to return a defective slave-girl when the seller claims the buyer was satisfied. The agent cannot return until the buyer swears, unlike the debt case where the agent can receive money without the creditor swearing.
The key distinction is the possibility of rectification (tadaruk) after the qadi's judgment.
2
Understand the principle of tadaruk
Recognize that tadaruk (rectification) is possible if the qadi's judgment is only externally effective. Abu Hanifa holds that in contracts and annulments, the judgment is effective both externally and internally, making tadaruk impossible. The Sahibayn hold it is only externally effective, so tadaruk is possible.
This principle is derived from their views on unrestricted gifts (amlak mursalah) in Kitab al-Nikah and al-Qada.
3
Compare Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa: The qadi's order to annul the sale is final. Even if error appears later (e.g., buyer refuses to swear and shows he was satisfied), the annulment stands. Therefore, the buyer is not sworn after the judgment because it would be useless.
The slave-girl cannot be returned to the buyer; the sale is irrevocably annulled.
4
Compare the Sahibayn's position
Sahibayn: The qadi's judgment is only externally effective. Thus, in both debt and defect cases, if the creditor/buyer later refuses to swear, the judgment can be annulled and the property returned. The agent can therefore proceed without the buyer's oath, and if the buyer later objects, the ruling is reversed.
The practical consequence: the buyer can recover the slave-girl if he swears he was not satisfied.
5
Evaluate Abu Yusuf's preferred view
Some scholars report that Abu Yusuf's correct view is to delay action in both cases until the oath is taken, out of consideration (nazar) for the seller/debtor. This protects the seller from losing his property if the buyer was actually satisfied and cannot be made to swear.
This view is considered more cautious and equitable.

اشرف الہدایہ جلد وہم
ہو کر قرض خواہ سے قسم لے گا کیونکہ قرضدار کی رعایت کرنا بھی ضروری ہے اور اس قسم دلانے میں بلاشبہ قرضدار کی رعایت ہے بہرحا ل قرض خواہ اگر یہ قسم کھا گیا کہ میں نے قرضہ کا مال وصول نہیں کیا ہے تو قرضدار سے جو مال وکیل کو دلایا گیا ہے اس سے قرضہ کی ادائیگی ہو جائے گی اور یہ اداء کرنا نافذ ہو جائیگا۔ اور اگر قرض خواہ نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیا تو قرضدار ، قابض یعنی وکیل کا دامن گیر ہوگا اور دیا ہوا مال واپس لے گا۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قرض خواہ کے بدلے وکیل سے قسم نہیں لی جائے گی اس لئے کہ وکیل اسکا نائب ہے اور ایمان میں نیابت فرماتےہیں نہیں لی ارکان ہےاور جاری نہیں ہوتی ۔

ترجمہ اگر کسی شخص کو باندی میں عیب کی وجہ سے (باندی) کو واپس کرنے کا وکیل کیا پھر بائع نے دعوی کیا مشتری کے راضی ہونے کا تو وکیل بائع پر واپس نہیں کر سکتا یہاں تک کہ مشتری سے قسم لی جائے۔ برخلاف مسئلہ قرض کے اس لئے کہ قرض کے مسئلہ میں تدارک ممکن ہے اس کو واپس لے کر جس پر وکیل نے قبضہ کیا ہے جبکہ قرض خواہ کے قسم سے انکار کے وقت خطأ ظاہر ہو گئی ہو اور دوسرے مسئلہ میں تدارک ممکن نہیں ہے کیونکہ ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نسخ پر فیصلہ کرنا صحت پر جاری ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ ان کا مذہب ہے اور اس کے بعد امام صاحب کے نزدیک مشتری سے قسم نہیں لی جائے گی کیونکہ یہ مفید نہیں ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک مشائخ نے کہا دونوں صورتوں میں حکم یکساں ہونا چاہئے۔ اور واپس کرنے کے حکم میں تاخیر نہ کی جائے۔ کیونکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک تدارک ممکن ہے اس لئے حکم قضا ، باطل ہے اور کہا گیا یہ ابو یوسف کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں مؤخر کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ انتظار معتبر ہے یہاں تک کہ مشتری سے قسم لی جائے۔ بشرطیکہ بائع کے دعوی کے بغیر وہ حاضر ہو تو غور کرنے کے لئے انتظار کیا جائے گا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے خریدی ہوئی باندی میں عیب پا کر ایک شخص کو بائع کی طرف باندی واپس کرنے کا وکیل کیا اور بائع نے دعوی کیا کہ مشتری اس عیب پر راضی ہو گیا تھا تو بحکم قضاء وکیل اس معیب باندی کو بائع کی طرف واپس نہیں کر سکتا یعنی قاضی اس باندی کو واپس کرنے کا حکم صادر نہیں کرے گا الا یہ کہ مشتری اس بات کی قسم کھائے کہ میں اس عیب پر راضی نہیں ہوا تھا اس کے

برخلاف قرضہ کا مسئلہ ہے کہ اگر قرضدار یہ دعوی کر دے کہ قرض خواہ اپنا قرضہ وصول کر چکا ہے تو قرض خواہ سے قسم لئے بغیر قرضدار کو حکم دیا جائے گا کہ مال قرض وکیل کو دے دے ان دونوں مسئلوں میں وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ مسئلہ قرض میں اگر قرض خواہ کے قسم کھانے سے انکار کرنے کی وجہ سے وکیل کو مال قرض دینے کا غلط ہونا ظاہر ہو گیا تو اس کا تدارک ممکن ہے اس طور پر کہ جو مال وکیل کو دیا گیا تھا قر ضد ار اس سے اس مال کو واپس لے لیگا اس لئے کہ قاضی کا یہ حکم کہ مال قرض وکیل کو دیدیا جائے ۔ صرف ظاہر ا نافذ ہوگا نہ کہ باطنا کیونکہ قاضی کا وکیل کو مال دینے کا حکم ایسا ہے جیسا کہ املاک مرسلہ میں قاضی کا حکم اور کتاب النکاح اور کتاب القضاء میں گذر چکا ہے کہ املاک مرسلہ میں قاضی کا حکم ظاہر انا فذ ہوتا ہے نہ کہ باطنا۔ پس جب یہاں قاضی کا حکم صرف ظاہر آنا فذ ہے اور باطنا نا فذ نہیں ہے تو وکیل سے اس مال کو واپس لینے میں کوئی دشواری پیش نہ آئے گی۔
اور دوسرے مسئلہ میں قاضی کی غلطی ظاہر ہونے کے بعد تدارک ممکن نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اگر قاضی نے بیع فخ کر دی اور مشتری سے قسم لئے بغیر معیب باندی بائع کو دیدی تو یہ بیچ مسخ ہی رہے گی اگر چہ ظاہر ہو جائے کہ فسخ کرنا غلط تھا کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک قضائے قاضی عقود و فسوخ میں ظاہراً اور باطنا دونوں طرح نافذ ہوتا ہے اور جب قاضی کا فیصلہ دونوں طرح نافذ ہو گیا تو قاضی کے ایک مرتبہ فسخ کرنے کے بعد اس فتح کو ختم نہیں کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ اگر چہ مشتری قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دے اور یہ بات ثابت ہو جائے کہ مشتری عیب پر راضی ہو چکا تھا بلکہ قاضی کے فتح کا حکم کرنے کے بعد مشتری سے تم نہیں کی جائیگی کیونکہ اب قسم لینا بے فائدہ ہے اور بے فائدہ اس لئے کہ جب قاضی بیع کو فسخ کر چکا تو مشتری اگر قسم کھانے سے انکار بھی کر دے اور عیب پر اس کی رضامندی ثابت بھی
ہو جائے تو بھی اس فتح کو ختم نہیں کیا جاسکتا ہے کیونکہ یہ نخ ظاہرا اور باطنا دونوں طرح نافذ ہو چکا۔
یہ خیال رہے کہ ان دونوں صورتوں میں مذکورہ فرق صرف امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے ورنہ صاحبین کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں ایک ہی حکم ہے یعنی مسئلہ قرض میں قرض خواہ سے قسم لئے بغیر مال قرض وکیل کو دلوادیا جائے گا اور مسئلہ رد بالعیب میں مشتری سے قسم لئے بغیر باندی بائع کو دیدی جائے گی۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دونوں صورتوں میں تدارک ممکن ہے کیونکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک قاضی کا حکم صرف ظاہرا نافذ ہوتا ہے اور باطنا نافذ نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذا اگر مشتری سے قسم لئے بغیر معیب باندی بائع کو دیدی گئی اور پھر مشتری نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیا تو قضائے قاضی کی خطاء ظاہر ہونے سے یہ معیب باندی بائع سے لے کر مشتری کو دیدی جائے گی اور قاضی کا مسخ بیع کا فیصلہ منسوخ کر دیا جائیگا اس لئے کہ قاضی کا حکم اگر ظاہر انا فذ ہو تو اس کو منسوخ کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ اور بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اصبح یہ ہے کہ دونوں صورتوں میں تاخیر کی جائے گی ۔ یعنی مسئلہ قرض میں قرض خواہ سے قسم لئے بغیر وکیل کو قرضہ کا مال نہ دیا جائے اور مسئلہ بیچ میں مشتری سے قسم لئے بغیر معیب باندی بائع کو واپس نہ کی جائے۔ کیونکہ امام ابو یوسف قرضدار اور بائع پر شفقت ملحوظ رکھتے ہیں اور شفقت کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ اگر مشتری موجود ہو اور معیب باندی ، بائع کی. طرف واپس کرنا چاہے تو مشتری سے قسم لئے بغیر معیب باندی بائع کی طرف واپس نہیں کی جائے گی اگر چہ بائع نے مشتری کے عیب پر راضی ہونے کا دعوی بھی نہ کیا ہو اسی طرح اگر مشتری غائب ہو تو بھی قسم لئے بغیر معیب باندی بائع کی طرف واپس نہیں کی جائے گی تا کہ قاضی کا فیصلہ بھی باطل ہونے سے محفوظ رہ سکے اور بائع پر شفقت بھی ملحوظ رہے اسی طرح پہلے مسئلہ میں قرض خواہ سے قسم لئے بغیر مال قرض وکیل کو نہ دیا جائے کیونکہ اس صورت میں قاضی کا فیصلہ بھی باطل ہونے سے محفوظ رہے گا اور قرضدار کے حق میں نظر و شفقت کا
Book of Agency. ... The author of Hidayah says: The agent will not be made to swear in place of the creditor, because the agent is his deputy, and deputyship is not valid in oaths... If someone appoints an agent to return a slave-girl due to a defect, and the seller claims that the buyer was satisfied with the defect, the agent cannot return it to the seller until the buyer swears [that he was not satisfied]. This is contrary to the debt case, because rectification is possible there by taking back what the agent had received when the error becomes apparent upon the creditor's refusal to swear. In the second case, rectification is not possible because the judgment of annulment is valid even if error becomes apparent, according to Abu Hanifa as is his madhhab. After that, the buyer is not made to swear in his view because it would be useless. As for the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), they said that the ruling should be the same in both cases and not delayed, because rectification is possible according to them due to the annulment of the judgment. And it is said that the correct view according to Abu Yusuf is to delay in both cases, because consideration is given to waiting until the buyer is made to swear if he were present without the seller's claim, so one waits for consideration. ... Summary: The difference between the two cases is that in the debt case, the qadi's order to give the money to the agent is effective only externally (zahiran) not internally (batina), so the money can be recovered. In the defect case, according to Abu Hanifa, the qadi's judgment of annulment is effective both externally and internally, so it cannot be reversed. According to the Sahibayn, both cases are similar because the qadi's judgment is only externally effective, so rectification is possible. Some scholars said that the correct view according to Abu Yusuf is to delay in both cases, out of consideration for the debtor and seller.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi legal dispute regarding the effect of a qadi's judgment in cases of agency for returning a defective slave-girl (jariyah) when the seller claims the buyer was satisfied with the defect. The text first establishes the ruling: if a person appoints an agent to return a defective slave-girl to the seller, and the seller claims that the buyer (the principal) was aware of and satisfied with the defect, the agent cannot return the slave-girl to the seller until the buyer swears that he was not satisfied. This is different from the debt case where the agent can receive the debt without the creditor swearing, because in the debt case rectification is possible: if the creditor later refuses to swear and the error becomes apparent, the money can be taken back from the agent. The reasoning is based on the nature of the qadi's judgment. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that in contracts and their annulments, the qadi's judgment is effective both outwardly and inwardly (zahiran wa batina). Therefore, once the qadi has ordered the annulment of the sale, it is final and cannot be undone, even if it later becomes clear that the judgment was erroneous (e.g., if the buyer refuses to swear and proves that he was satisfied). Thus, after the qadi's judgment, there is no benefit in asking the buyer to swear. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the qadi's judgment is only effective outwardly, not inwardly. Therefore, in both the debt and defect cases, rectification is possible. If the buyer later refuses to swear, the qadi's judgment can be annulled and the slave-girl can be returned to the buyer. Some scholars report that the correct view according to Abu Yusuf is to delay action in both cases until the buyer (or creditor) is made to swear, in order to protect the interests of the debtor and seller. This passage thus illustrates how a difference in the underlying principle (the scope of a qadi's judgment) leads to different practical rulings. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is not explicitly stated, but the text presents the views of the three imams.

Key Terms
الوكالة (al-wakalah): The contract of agency, where one person appoints another to act on his behalf in a specific matter, such as returning a defective slave-girl.
تدارك (tadaruk): Rectification or remedy; the possibility of undoing or correcting a legal action that was wrongly performed, e.g., recovering property given under a mistaken judgment.
قضاء القاضي (qada' al-qadi): The judgment of a judge; its effect can be either only externally (zahiran) or both externally and internally (zahiran wa batina), which determines whether it can be annulled if found erroneous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), why is the defective slave-girl case similar to the debt case?
A) Because in both cases, the qadi's judgment is effective both externally and internally.
B) Because in both cases, rectification (tadaruk) is possible since the qadi's judgment is only externally effective.
C) Because the buyer's oath is always required before any return.
D) Because the agent has no authority in either case.

Key Takeaway
The effect of a qadi's judgment—whether final or reversible—depends on the underlying principle: if the judgment is effective both externally and internally, it is irreversible; if only externally, it can be rectified. This principle yields different rulings within the Hanafi school.

Requirements for a Valid Claim: Attendance, Response, and Movable Property
Explains essential elements for a valid da'wa: attendance, response, movable property presentation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four wajibat for a valid claim in Hanafi law and identify which shurut must be satisfied for a claim of movable property.

Core Idea
A valid claim requires defendant's attendance, response, presentation of movables, and oath upon denial.

This lesson covers the fundamental procedural requirements for a valid claim (da'wa) in Hanafi law. The text from Ashraf al-Hidayah details what the plaintiff and defendant must do: the defendant must attend court, respond to the claim, produce the claimed movable property (or state its value and gender if absent), and take an oath if evidence is lacking. Understanding these elements is essential for any legal practitioner working within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wajibat of a valid claim
List the four obligatory elements mentioned: defendant's attendance, defendant's response, presentation of movable property (or statement of value/gender), and defendant's oath upon denial.
The text also mentions that attendance is wajib based on practice of Companions and Quran 24:48.
2
Understand the evidence for attendance
The text cites Quran 24:48 and the consensus of the Companions as proof that the defendant must appear in court.
The dalil is Quranic but its indication (dalala) is zanni, making attendance wajib not fard.
3
Analyze the requirements for movable property
If the claimed object is movable and in defendant's possession, it must be physically produced in court for pointing. If lost/destroyed, the plaintiff must state its value and gender (per Abu al-Layth).
Description alone is insufficient due to commonality in attributes.
4
Distinguish shurut from arkan
Shurut include proper identification of the object and possession by defendant. Arkan include plaintiff’s statement and defendant’s response.
Omission of a rukn invalidates the claim; omission of a wajib (e.g., attendance) may be compelled but does not void the claim.

حاضر ہونا اول سے آخر تک ہر زمانے کے قاضی اسی قول پر چلتے آئے ہیں اور جواب کا واجب ہونا جب مدعی علیہ حاضر ہوتا کہ اس کی حاضری مفید ہو اور مال منقول جس میں دعوئی واقع ہوا ہے اس کو حاضر کرنا لازم ہے دلیل وہی ہے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے۔ اور مدعی علیہ جب دعوی کا انکار کر دے یمین لازم ہے اس کو انشاء اللہ عنقریب ذکر کریں گے اور اگر وہ مال منقول حاضر نہ ہو تو اس کی قیمت ذکر کر دے تا کہ مدعی (جس کا دعوی کیا گیا ہے ) معلوم ہو سکے اس لئے کہ مال منقول وصف کے ذریعہ معلوم نہیں ہو سکتا ہے اور قیمت کے ذریعہ شناخت ہو سکتی ہے حالانکہ مال عین کا مشاہدہ کرنا متعذر ہے فقیہ ابواللیث نے کہا کہ قیمت بیان کرنے کے ساتھ مذکر اور مؤنث ہونے کا ذکر کرنا بھی شرط ہے۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ مدعی کا دعوی اس وقت قبول ہو گا جب وہ اس شی کی جنس اور مقدار ذکر کر دئے جس کا دعوی کیا گیا ہے مثلاً یہ کہے کہ میرے فلاں آدمی پر ایک سو دینار ہیں ایک سو درہم ہیں ایک کر گندم ہے کیونکہ دعوی کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ حجت قائم کر کے مدعی علیہ پر مدعی کا حق لازم کیا جائے اور مجبول چیز کا لازم کرنا چونکہ ممکن نہیں ہے اس لئے شی مدعی بہ کی جنس اور مقدار کا بیان کرنا ضروری ہے۔
صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ اگر مدعی بہ (جس کا دعوی کیا گیا ہے ) مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ میں مال عین منقول ہو، تو مدعی علیہ کو تکلیف دی جائے گی کہ وہ اس مال کو عدالت قاضی میں حاضر کرے تا کہ مدعی ، دعوی کرتے وقت اس مال کی طرف اشارہ کر سکے اسی طرح اگر گواہوں نے گواہی دی یا مدعی علیہ سے قسم لی گئی تو مدعی علیہ کو زحمت دی جائے گی کہ وہ مال مدعلی بہ کو حاضر کرے تا کہ گواہ ادائے شہادت کے وقت اسکی طرف اشارہ کر سکے اسی طرح اگر گواہوں نے گواہی دی یا مدعلی علیہ سے قسم لی گئی تو مدعلی علیہ کو زحمت دی جائے گی کہ وہ مال مدعی بہ کو حاضر کرے تا کہ گواہ ادائے شہادت کے وقت اس کی طرف اشارہ کر سکیں اور مدعی علیہ قسم کے وقت اشارہ کر سکے ۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ مدعی بہ کے بارے میں جہاں تک ممکن ہو آگاہ کرنا شرط ہے اور ایسی آگا ہی مال منقول میں اشارہ سے ہوتی ہے کیونکہ مال منقول عدالت میں منتقل کرنا بھی ممکن ہے اور اشارہ سے شناخت غایت درجہ کی ہوتی ہے اس لئے کہ اشارہ کرنا تو ایسا ہے جیسے کسی چیز پر ہاتھ رکھ دیا ہو اور ہاتھ رکھنے کے بعد شناخت میں کیا شبہ ہو سکتا ہے۔ بہر حال اشارہ کرنے کیلئے اس کی مدعی بہ کا مجلس قاضی میں حاضر کرنا ضروری ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ دعوی صحیحہ کے ساتھ چند امور متعلق ہوتے ہیں۔ مدعی علیہ پر مجلس قاضی میں حاضر ہونا واجب ہے ہر زمانہ کے قاضیوں کا عمل بھی اسی پر ہے۔ چنانچہ حضرت عمر ، عثمان علی اور صحابہ کے بعد تابعین نے اس پر عمل کیا ہے اور کسی نے نکیر نہیں کی اور ابن ابی لیلی یہی عمل کرتے تھے مگر ابوحنیفہ نے نکیر نہیں کی پس یہ اجتماع کے قائم مقام ہے اور اس سلسلہ میں اصل باری تعالیٰ کا یہ قول ہے۔
وإِذَا دُعُوا إِلَى اللَّهِ وَرَسُولِه لِيَحْكُمْ بَيْنَهُمُ إِذَا فَرِيقٌ مِّنْهُمْ مُعْرِضُونَ یعنی جب ان کو اللہ اور اس کے رسول کی طرف بلایا جائے تا کہ وہ ان کے درمیان فیصلہ کرے تو ایک فریق ان میں سے اعراض کرتا ہے۔

۲۔ جب مدعی علیہ حاضر ہو تو اس پر نعم یا لا کے ساتھ جواب دینا واجب ہے تا کہ اس کی حاضری سودمند ثابت ہو کیونکہ مدعی کی حاضری کا مقصد ہی جواب دہی کرنا ہے۔
- مال منقول جس میں دعوی واقع ہوا ہے سابقہ دلیل کی وجہ سے اس کا مجلس قاضی میں حاضر کر نالازم ہے۔ ۴۔ اور مدعی علیہ اگر دعوی کا انکار کر دے اور مدعی بینہ پیش کرنے سے عاجز ہو جائے تو مدعی علیہ پر پہین لا زم ہے لزوم یہین کا بیان ان شاء اللہ اس باب کے آخیر میں آئے گا۔
صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ اگر مال منقول جس کا دعوی کیا گیا ہے مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ میں موجود نہ ہو بلکہ تلف ہو گیا یا غائب ہو گیا جسن کا ٹھکا نہ معلوم نہیں ہے تو اس صورت میں مدعی اس مال کی قیمت ذکر کر دے تاکہ مدعی معلوم ہو کر دعوی درست ہو جائے اس صورت میں وصف کا بیان کرنا کافی نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وصف بھی بہت سے اعیان کے درمیان مشترک ہوتا ہے تو اشتراک کی وجہ سے وصف کے ذریعہ معین شی کی شناخت نہ ہو سکے گی اور جب ایسا ہے تو اس اشتراک کی وجہ سے وصف کا بیان مفید ثابت نہ ہوگا اور رہی قیمت تو اس کے ذریعہ شی کی شناخت ہو سکتی ہے پس جب قیمت کے ذریعہ شی کی شناخت ہو سکتی ہے۔ اور عین شی کا مشاہدہ کرنا متعذ رہے تو قیمت کا ذکر کرنا مفید ہوگا کیونکہ ایسی صورت میں قیمت کا ذکر ہی آگاہی کا آخری امکانی درجہ ہے۔
فقیہ ابواللیث نے کہا کہ مذکورہ صورت میں بیان قیمت کے ساتھ یہ بیان کرنا بھی ضروری ہے کہ وہ چیز جس کا دعوی کیا گیا ہے مذکر ہے یا مؤنث ہے۔
زمین کے دعوی کیلئے زمین کی حدودار بعد بیان کرے
قال فان ادعى عقارا حدده وذكر انه فى يد المدعى عليه وانه يطالبه به لانه تعذر التعريف بالاشارة لتعذر النقل فيصار الى التحديد فان العقار يعرف به ويذكر الحدود الاربعة ويذكر اسماء أصحاب الحدود وانسابهم ولابد من ذكر الجد لان تمام التعريف به عند ابي حنيفة على ما عرف هو الصحيح ولو كان الرجل مشهورا يكتفى بذكره فان ذكر ثلثة من الحدود يكتفى بها عندنا خلافا لزفر لوجود الاكثر بخلاف ما اذا غلط فى الرابعة لانه يختلف به المدعى ولا كذالك بتركها وكما يشترط التحديد في الدعوى يشترط في الشهادة وقوله فى الكتاب وذكر انه فى يد المدعى عليه لابد منه لأنه انما ينتصب خصما اذا كان في يده وفى العقار لا يكتفى بذكر المدعى وتصديق المدعى عليه انه فى يده بل لا يثبت اليد فيه الا بالبينة او علم القاضى هو الصحيح نفيا لتهمة المواضعة اذ العقار عساه في يد غيرهما بخلاف المنقول لان اليد فيه مشاهدة وقوله وانه يطالبه به لان المطالبة حقه فلا بد من طلبه ولانه يحتمل ان يكون مرهونا في يده او محبوسا بالثمن في يده وبالمطالبة يزول هذا الاحتمال وعن هذا قالوا فى المنقول يجب أن يقول في يده بغیر حق قال وان كان حقا في الذمة ذكر انه يطالبه به لما قلنا وهذا لان صاحب الذمة قد حضر فلم يبق الا المطالبة لكن لا بد من تعريفه بالوصف لانه يعرف به
ترجمہ اور اگر مدعی نے کسی غیر منقول چیز کا دعوی کیا تو مدعی اس کے حدود بیان کرے اور یہ بھی بیان کرے کہ وہ مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ
Book of Claims. Ashraf al-Bidayah Volume - 10. The defendant's presence from beginning to end; judges of every age have acted upon this statement. And the obligation of a response when the defendant is present so that his presence is beneficial. And it is necessary to produce the movable property concerning which the claim is made; the proof is that which we have already stated. And when the defendant denies the claim, an oath is necessary; we will mention this soon, God willing. And if the movable property is not present, let him state its value so that the plaintiff (the one who claims) can be known, because movable property cannot be known by description, but can be identified by its value, while direct observation of the property is impossible. Faqih Abu al-Layth said: along with stating the value, it is also a condition to mention whether the item is masculine or feminine. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that the plaintiff's claim is accepted only when he mentions the genus and quantity of the thing claimed, for example saying: 'So-and-so owes me one hundred dinars, one hundred dirhams, or one kurr of wheat,' because the benefit of the claim is to establish proof and obligate the plaintiff's right upon the defendant, and since it is not possible to obligate an unknown thing, it is necessary to state the genus and quantity of the claimed object. Sahib al-Quduri says: If the claimed object is a movable corporeal property in the possession of the defendant, the defendant will be required to present that property in the court of the judge so that the plaintiff can point to it when making the claim. Similarly, if witnesses testify or the defendant is made to take an oath, the defendant will be burdened to present the claimed property so that the witnesses can point to it when giving testimony and the defendant can point to it when taking the oath. The proof for this is that it is a condition to inform about the claimed property as much as possible, and such information in movable property is achieved by pointing, because it is possible to transport movable property to court, and identification by pointing is the utmost degree, because pointing is like placing a hand on something, and after placing a hand, what doubt can there be in identification? In any case, for pointing, it is necessary to present the claimed object in the judge's court. Sahib al-Hidayah says that several matters are connected to a valid claim: It is obligatory for the defendant to attend the judge's court; the practice of judges of all ages is upon this. Thus, Umar, Uthman, Ali, and after the Companions, the Tabi'un acted upon this, and no one disapproved. Ibn Abi Layla used to act upon this, and Abu Hanifah did not disapprove. So this stands in place of consensus. And the basis for this is the saying of Allah Almighty: 'And when they are called to Allah and His Messenger to judge between them, at once a party of them turn away.' [Quran 24:48] Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume - 10. Book of Claims. 2. When the defendant is present, it is obligatory for him to reply with 'yes' or 'no', so that his presence proves beneficial, because the purpose of the plaintiff's presence is to obtain a response. 3. The movable property concerning which the claim is made must be presented in the judge's court due to the earlier proof. 4. And if the defendant denies the claim and the plaintiff is unable to provide evidence, then the taking of an oath becomes obligatory upon the defendant; the explanation of the necessity of the oath will come at the end of this chapter, God willing. Sahib al-Quduri said: If the movable object that is claimed is not present in the possession of the defendant, but rather has been destroyed or lost, and its location is unknown, then in that case the plaintiff should state its value so that the plaintiff becomes known and the claim is valid. In this case, stating the description will not suffice, because description is common to many objects, and due to this commonality, identification of a specific object cannot be achieved through description. When that is the case, stating the description will not be beneficial. As for value, through it the object can be identified. So when identification through value is possible, and direct observation of the object itself is impossible, then stating the value will be beneficial, because in such a case, stating the value is the final possible degree of information. Faqih Abu al-Layth said: In the mentioned case, along with stating the value, it is also necessary to state whether the object claimed is masculine or feminine. For a claim of land, he should state the boundaries of the land. He said: If he claims immovable property, he must define it and mention that it is in the possession of the defendant and that he is demanding it from him, because identification by pointing is impossible due to the impossibility of transporting it, so one resorts to defining boundaries, since immovable property is known by that. He should mention the four boundaries and the names of the owners of the boundaries and their genealogies. It is necessary to mention the grandfather, because complete identification is through him according to Abu Hanifah, as is known to be correct. If the person is well-known, mentioning him suffices. If he mentions only three of the boundaries, it suffices according to us, contrary to Zufar, because the majority is present, unlike if he makes a mistake in the fourth, because the claim changes due to it, and not so by omitting it. Just as defining boundaries is required in the claim, it is also required in testimony. And his statement in the book: 'and mention that it is in the possession of the defendant' is necessary, because he only becomes a defendant if it is in his possession. Regarding immovable property, it is not sufficient to rely on the plaintiff's statement and the defendant's confirmation that it is in his possession; rather, possession is established only by evidence or the judge's knowledge; this is the correct view to eliminate suspicion of collusion, because immovable property might be in someone else's possession, unlike movable property, because possession of it is observable. And his statement: 'and he is demanding it from him' because demand is his right, so he must demand it, and because it is possible that it is in his possession as a mortgage or held for the price, and by demanding, this possibility is removed. Regarding this, they said regarding movable property, he must say 'in his possession without right'. He said: and if it is a debt in the liability, he mentions that he demands it from him for what we have said. This is because the debtor is present, so nothing remains except the demand. But it is necessary to define it by description because it is known by that. Translation: And if the plaintiff claims something non-movable, the plaintiff should mention its boundaries and also mention that it is in the possession of the defendant.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, a commentary on al-Hidayah by Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani, discusses the requirements for a valid claim (da'wa) in Hanafi fiqh. The text is a ruling_statement with proofs, explaining the essential elements for a claim to be accepted in court. The author begins by stating that the defendant must attend court—a practice established by the Companions and accepted by consensus (ijma), supported by Quran 24:48 which implies obedience to the Prophet's judgment. Then, the defendant must reply 'yes' or 'no' to the claim, otherwise attendance is useless. For movable property, the item must be physically presented in court so the plaintiff can point to it, as pointing gives certain identification. If the property is lost or absent, the plaintiff must state its value and gender (per Faqih Abu al-Layth) because description alone is insufficient due to commonality. For immovable property, since it cannot be transported, the plaintiff must define its boundaries—specifying four boundaries, names of neighbors and their genealogy (including grandfather) according to Abu Hanifah. Mentioning three boundaries suffices per Hanafis, contrary to Zufar. Possession of immovable property must be proven by evidence or judicial knowledge, not just by assertion, to prevent collusion. The demand (matalaba) must be explicit to clarify the right and remove doubt. This lesson covers the core procedural rules for both movable and immovable claims.

Key Terms
دعوى (da'wa): A claim made by a plaintiff against a defendant before a judge, seeking to establish a right.
مدعی علیہ (mudda'a 'alayh): The defendant against whom the claim is made.
حدود (hudud): Boundaries or limits of immovable property, which must be specified in a claim for land.
یمین (yamin): Oath taken by the defendant when the plaintiff lacks evidence after denial.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ashraf al-Hidayah, what is the consequence if the defendant refuses to attend court without a valid excuse?
A) The claim becomes batil (invalid)
B) The judge may compel attendance, but the claim remains valid
C) The plaintiff automatically wins the case
D) The defendant must pay a fine

Key Takeaway
The core of a valid claim is clear identification of the subject matter, either by presentation or description with value and gender.

Requirements for a Valid Claim: Immovable Property and Boundary Definition
Explains specific rules for immovable property claims: boundaries, possession proof, and demand.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirements for claiming immovable property, including boundary specification, possession proof, and the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of boundaries needed.

Core Idea
Immovable property claims require precise boundary definition (four boundaries, with three sufficing per Hanafis) and proof of possession by evidence.

This lesson focuses on the specific rules for claiming immovable property ( العقار) as outlined in Ashraf al-Hidayah. Since immovable property cannot be physically produced in court, the law requires the plaintiff to define the property by mentioning its four boundaries, the names and genealogies of the neighboring owners, and to prove that the defendant is in possession. The text also discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Zufar required all four boundaries, while the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) accept three.

Guided Path
1
Understand why boundaries are used instead of pointing
Immovable property cannot be transported to court, so identification must be done by defining its boundaries (hudud).
The text states: 'because identification by pointing is impossible due to the impossibility of transporting it, so one resorts to defining boundaries.'
2
List the required elements of boundary definition
The plaintiff must mention four boundaries, the names of the boundary owners, and their genealogies (including grandfather). If a neighbor is well-known, naming him suffices.
Mentioning the grandfather is necessary for complete identification according to Abu Hanifa.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on boundaries
The majority holds that mentioning three boundaries suffices ('indana), while Zufar required all four. The text argues that the majority is sufficient.
Mistake in the fourth boundary changes the claim, but omitting it does not.
4
Recognize the rules for possession of immovable property
Possession must be proven by evidence (bayyina) or judicial knowledge; it cannot be based solely on the plaintiff's assertion or the defendant's confirmation, to prevent collusion.
This contrasts with movable property where possession is observable.
5
Understand the requirement of demand (matalaba)
The plaintiff must explicitly demand the property from the defendant, to eliminate possibilities like mortgage or lien.
The text says: 'because demand is his right, so he must demand it.'

حاضر ہونا اول سے آخر تک ہر زمانے کے قاضی اسی قول پر چلتے آئے ہیں اور جواب کا واجب ہونا جب مدعی علیہ حاضر ہوتا کہ اس کی حاضری مفید ہو اور مال منقول جس میں دعوئی واقع ہوا ہے اس کو حاضر کرنا لازم ہے دلیل وہی ہے جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے۔ اور مدعی علیہ جب دعوی کا انکار کر دے یمین لازم ہے اس کو انشاء اللہ عنقریب ذکر کریں گے اور اگر وہ مال منقول حاضر نہ ہو تو اس کی قیمت ذکر کر دے تا کہ مدعی (جس کا دعوی کیا گیا ہے ) معلوم ہو سکے اس لئے کہ مال منقول وصف کے ذریعہ معلوم نہیں ہو سکتا ہے اور قیمت کے ذریعہ شناخت ہو سکتی ہے حالانکہ مال عین کا مشاہدہ کرنا متعذر ہے فقیہ ابواللیث نے کہا کہ قیمت بیان کرنے کے ساتھ مذکر اور مؤنث ہونے کا ذکر کرنا بھی شرط ہے۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ مدعی کا دعوی اس وقت قبول ہو گا جب وہ اس شی کی جنس اور مقدار ذکر کر دئے جس کا دعوی کیا گیا ہے مثلاً یہ کہے کہ میرے فلاں آدمی پر ایک سو دینار ہیں ایک سو درہم ہیں ایک کر گندم ہے کیونکہ دعوی کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ حجت قائم کر کے مدعی علیہ پر مدعی کا حق لازم کیا جائے اور مجبول چیز کا لازم کرنا چونکہ ممکن نہیں ہے اس لئے شی مدعی بہ کی جنس اور مقدار کا بیان کرنا ضروری ہے۔
صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ اگر مدعی بہ (جس کا دعوی کیا گیا ہے ) مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ میں مال عین منقول ہو، تو مدعی علیہ کو تکلیف دی جائے گی کہ وہ اس مال کو عدالت قاضی میں حاضر کرے تا کہ مدعی ، دعوی کرتے وقت اس مال کی طرف اشارہ کر سکے اسی طرح اگر گواہوں نے گواہی دی یا مدعی علیہ سے قسم لی گئی تو مدعی علیہ کو زحمت دی جائے گی کہ وہ مال مدعلی بہ کو حاضر کرے تا کہ گواہ ادائے شہادت کے وقت اسکی طرف اشارہ کر سکے اسی طرح اگر گواہوں نے گواہی دی یا مدعلی علیہ سے قسم لی گئی تو مدعلی علیہ کو زحمت دی جائے گی کہ وہ مال مدعی بہ کو حاضر کرے تا کہ گواہ ادائے شہادت کے وقت اس کی طرف اشارہ کر سکیں اور مدعی علیہ قسم کے وقت اشارہ کر سکے ۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ مدعی بہ کے بارے میں جہاں تک ممکن ہو آگاہ کرنا شرط ہے اور ایسی آگا ہی مال منقول میں اشارہ سے ہوتی ہے کیونکہ مال منقول عدالت میں منتقل کرنا بھی ممکن ہے اور اشارہ سے شناخت غایت درجہ کی ہوتی ہے اس لئے کہ اشارہ کرنا تو ایسا ہے جیسے کسی چیز پر ہاتھ رکھ دیا ہو اور ہاتھ رکھنے کے بعد شناخت میں کیا شبہ ہو سکتا ہے۔ بہر حال اشارہ کرنے کیلئے اس کی مدعی بہ کا مجلس قاضی میں حاضر کرنا ضروری ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ دعوی صحیحہ کے ساتھ چند امور متعلق ہوتے ہیں۔ مدعی علیہ پر مجلس قاضی میں حاضر ہونا واجب ہے ہر زمانہ کے قاضیوں کا عمل بھی اسی پر ہے۔ چنانچہ حضرت عمر ، عثمان علی اور صحابہ کے بعد تابعین نے اس پر عمل کیا ہے اور کسی نے نکیر نہیں کی اور ابن ابی لیلی یہی عمل کرتے تھے مگر ابوحنیفہ نے نکیر نہیں کی پس یہ اجتماع کے قائم مقام ہے اور اس سلسلہ میں اصل باری تعالیٰ کا یہ قول ہے۔

كتاب الدعوى
۲۔ جب مدعی علیہ حاضر ہو تو اس پر نعم یا لا کے ساتھ جواب دینا واجب ہے تا کہ اس کی حاضری سودمند ثابت ہو کیونکہ مدعی کی حاضری کا مقصد ہی جواب دہی کرنا ہے۔
- مال منقول جس میں دعوی واقع ہوا ہے سابقہ دلیل کی وجہ سے اس کا مجلس قاضی میں حاضر کر نالازم ہے۔ ۴۔ اور مدعی علیہ اگر دعوی کا انکار کر دے اور مدعی بینہ پیش کرنے سے عاجز ہو جائے تو مدعی علیہ پر پہین لا زم ہے لزوم یہین کا بیان ان شاء اللہ اس باب کے آخیر میں آئے گا۔
صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ اگر مال منقول جس کا دعوی کیا گیا ہے مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ میں موجود نہ ہو بلکہ تلف ہو گیا یا غائب ہو گیا جسن کا ٹھکا نہ معلوم نہیں ہے تو اس صورت میں مدعی اس مال کی قیمت ذکر کر دے تاکہ مدعی معلوم ہو کر دعوی درست ہو جائے اس صورت میں وصف کا بیان کرنا کافی نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وصف بھی بہت سے اعیان کے درمیان مشترک ہوتا ہے تو اشتراک کی وجہ سے وصف کے ذریعہ معین شی کی شناخت نہ ہو سکے گی اور جب ایسا ہے تو اس اشتراک کی وجہ سے وصف کا بیان مفید ثابت نہ ہوگا اور رہی قیمت تو اس کے ذریعہ شی کی شناخت ہو سکتی ہے پس جب قیمت کے ذریعہ شی کی شناخت ہو سکتی ہے۔ اور عین شی کا مشاہدہ کرنا متعذ رہے تو قیمت کا ذکر کرنا مفید ہوگا کیونکہ ایسی صورت میں قیمت کا ذکر ہی آگاہی کا آخری امکانی درجہ ہے۔
فقیہ ابواللیث نے کہا کہ مذکورہ صورت میں بیان قیمت کے ساتھ یہ بیان کرنا بھی ضروری ہے کہ وہ چیز جس کا دعوی کیا گیا ہے مذکر ہے یا مؤنث ہے۔
زمین کے دعوی کیلئے زمین کی حدودار بعد بیان کرے
قال فان ادعى عقارا حدده وذكر انه فى يد المدعى عليه وانه يطالبه به لانه تعذر التعريف بالاشارة لتعذر النقل فيصار الى التحديد فان العقار يعرف به ويذكر الحدود الاربعة ويذكر اسماء أصحاب الحدود وانسابهم ولابد من ذكر الجد لان تمام التعريف به عند ابي حنيفة على ما عرف هو الصحيح ولو كان الرجل مشهورا يكتفى بذكره فان ذكر ثلثة من الحدود يكتفى بها عندنا خلافا لزفر لوجود الاكثر بخلاف ما اذا غلط فى الرابعة لانه يختلف به المدعى ولا كذالك بتركها وكما يشترط التحديد في الدعوى يشترط في الشهادة وقوله فى الكتاب وذكر انه فى يد المدعى عليه لابد منه لأنه انما ينتصب خصما اذا كان في يده وفى العقار لا يكتفى بذكر المدعى وتصديق المدعى عليه انه فى يده بل لا يثبت اليد فيه الا بالبينة او علم القاضى هو الصحيح نفيا لتهمة المواضعة اذ العقار عساه في يد غيرهما بخلاف المنقول لان اليد فيه مشاهدة وقوله وانه يطالبه به لان المطالبة حقه فلا بد من طلبه ولانه يحتمل ان يكون مرهونا في يده او محبوسا بالثمن في يده وبالمطالبة يزول هذا الاحتمال وعن هذا قالوا فى المنقول يجب أن يقول في يده بغیر حق قال وان كان حقا في الذمة ذكر انه يطالبه به لما قلنا وهذا لان صاحب الذمة قد حضر فلم يبق الا المطالبة لكن لا بد من تعريفه بالوصف لانه يعرف به
ترجمہ اور اگر مدعی نے کسی غیر منقول چیز کا دعوی کیا تو مدعی اس کے حدود بیان کرے اور یہ بھی بیان کرے کہ وہ مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ
Book of Claims. Ashraf al-Bidayah Volume - 10. The defendant's presence from beginning to end; judges of every age have acted upon this statement. And the obligation of a response when the defendant is present so that his presence is beneficial. And it is necessary to produce the movable property concerning which the claim is made; the proof is that which we have already stated. And when the defendant denies the claim, an oath is necessary; we will mention this soon, God willing. And if the movable property is not present, let him state its value so that the plaintiff (the one who claims) can be known, because movable property cannot be known by description, but can be identified by its value, while direct observation of the property is impossible. Faqih Abu al-Layth said: along with stating the value, it is also a condition to mention whether the item is masculine or feminine. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that the plaintiff's claim is accepted only when he mentions the genus and quantity of the thing claimed, for example saying: 'So-and-so owes me one hundred dinars, one hundred dirhams, or one kurr of wheat,' because the benefit of the claim is to establish proof and obligate the plaintiff's right upon the defendant, and since it is not possible to obligate an unknown thing, it is necessary to state the genus and quantity of the claimed object. Sahib al-Quduri says: If the claimed object is a movable corporeal property in the possession of the defendant, the defendant will be required to present that property in the court of the judge so that the plaintiff can point to it when making the claim. Similarly, if witnesses testify or the defendant is made to take an oath, the defendant will be burdened to present the claimed property so that the witnesses can point to it when giving testimony and the defendant can point to it when taking the oath. The proof for this is that it is a condition to inform about the claimed property as much as possible, and such information in movable property is achieved by pointing, because it is possible to transport movable property to court, and identification by pointing is the utmost degree, because pointing is like placing a hand on something, and after placing a hand, what doubt can there be in identification? In any case, for pointing, it is necessary to present the claimed object in the judge's court. Sahib al-Hidayah says that several matters are connected to a valid claim: It is obligatory for the defendant to attend the judge's court; the practice of judges of all ages is upon this. Thus, Umar, Uthman, Ali, and after the Companions, the Tabi'un acted upon this, and no one disapproved. Ibn Abi Layla used to act upon this, and Abu Hanifah did not disapprove. So this stands in place of consensus. And the basis for this is the saying of Allah Almighty: 'And when they are called to Allah and His Messenger to judge between them, at once a party of them turn away.' [Quran 24:48] Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume - 10. Book of Claims. 2. When the defendant is present, it is obligatory for him to reply with 'yes' or 'no', so that his presence proves beneficial, because the purpose of the plaintiff's presence is to obtain a response. 3. The movable property concerning which the claim is made must be presented in the judge's court due to the earlier proof. 4. And if the defendant denies the claim and the plaintiff is unable to provide evidence, then the taking of an oath becomes obligatory upon the defendant; the explanation of the necessity of the oath will come at the end of this chapter, God willing. Sahib al-Quduri said: If the movable object that is claimed is not present in the possession of the defendant, but rather has been destroyed or lost, and its location is unknown, then in that case the plaintiff should state its value so that the plaintiff becomes known and the claim is valid. In this case, stating the description will not suffice, because description is common to many objects, and due to this commonality, identification of a specific object cannot be achieved through description. When that is the case, stating the description will not be beneficial. As for value, through it the object can be identified. So when identification through value is possible, and direct observation of the object itself is impossible, then stating the value will be beneficial, because in such a case, stating the value is the final possible degree of information. Faqih Abu al-Layth said: In the mentioned case, along with stating the value, it is also necessary to state whether the object claimed is masculine or feminine. For a claim of land, he should state the boundaries of the land. He said: If he claims immovable property, he must define it and mention that it is in the possession of the defendant and that he is demanding it from him, because identification by pointing is impossible due to the impossibility of transporting it, so one resorts to defining boundaries, since immovable property is known by that. He should mention the four boundaries and the names of the owners of the boundaries and their genealogies. It is necessary to mention the grandfather, because complete identification is through him according to Abu Hanifah, as is known to be correct. If the person is well-known, mentioning him suffices. If he mentions only three of the boundaries, it suffices according to us, contrary to Zufar, because the majority is present, unlike if he makes a mistake in the fourth, because the claim changes due to it, and not so by omitting it. Just as defining boundaries is required in the claim, it is also required in testimony. And his statement in the book: 'and mention that it is in the possession of the defendant' is necessary, because he only becomes a defendant if it is in his possession. Regarding immovable property, it is not sufficient to rely on the plaintiff's statement and the defendant's confirmation that it is in his possession; rather, possession is established only by evidence or the judge's knowledge; this is the correct view to eliminate suspicion of collusion, because immovable property might be in someone else's possession, unlike movable property, because possession of it is observable. And his statement: 'and he is demanding it from him' because demand is his right, so he must demand it, and because it is possible that it is in his possession as a mortgage or held for the price, and by demanding, this possibility is removed. Regarding this, they said regarding movable property, he must say 'in his possession without right'. He said: and if it is a debt in the liability, he mentions that he demands it from him for what we have said. This is because the debtor is present, so nothing remains except the demand. But it is necessary to define it by description because it is known by that. Translation: And if the plaintiff claims something non-movable, the plaintiff should mention its boundaries and also mention that it is in the possession of the defendant.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, a commentary on al-Hidayah by Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani, discusses the requirements for a valid claim (da'wa) in Hanafi fiqh. The text is a ruling_statement with proofs, explaining the essential elements for a claim to be accepted in court. The author begins by stating that the defendant must attend court—a practice established by the Companions and accepted by consensus (ijma), supported by Quran 24:48 which implies obedience to the Prophet's judgment. Then, the defendant must reply 'yes' or 'no' to the claim, otherwise attendance is useless. For movable property, the item must be physically presented in court so the plaintiff can point to it, as pointing gives certain identification. If the property is lost or absent, the plaintiff must state its value and gender (per Faqih Abu al-Layth) because description alone is insufficient due to commonality. For immovable property, since it cannot be transported, the plaintiff must define its boundaries—specifying four boundaries, names of neighbors and their genealogy (including grandfather) according to Abu Hanifah. Mentioning three boundaries suffices per Hanafis, contrary to Zufar. Possession of immovable property must be proven by evidence or judicial knowledge, not just by assertion, to prevent collusion. The demand (matalaba) must be explicit to clarify the right and remove doubt. This lesson covers the core procedural rules for both movable and immovable claims.

Key Terms
دعوى (da'wa): A claim made by a plaintiff against a defendant before a judge, seeking to establish a right.
مدعی علیہ (mudda'a 'alayh): The defendant against whom the claim is made.
حدود (hudud): Boundaries or limits of immovable property, which must be specified in a claim for land.
یمین (yamin): Oath taken by the defendant when the plaintiff lacks evidence after denial.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi majority, how many boundaries must be mentioned for a claim of immovable property to be valid?
A) All four boundaries are required
B) At least three boundaries suffice
C) Two boundaries are sufficient if the property is well-known
D) Only the east and west boundaries need to be stated

Key Takeaway
A valid claim for immovable property requires specification of at least three boundaries, proof of the defendant's possession, and an explicit demand.

Three Conditions for a Lawsuit on Immovable Property
Ruling with proof on conditions for immovable property lawsuits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three necessary conditions for a valid claim on immovable property under Hanafi law and apply the requirement to prove possession with evidence rather than mere assertion.

Core Idea
A claim on immovable property requires boundary definition, proof of possession, and explicit demand—ensuring certainty and preventing collusion.

In this passage from Kitab al-Da'wa, the Hanafi school lays out three procedural requirements for a lawsuit involving immovable property like land or a house. Unlike movable property, which can be physically presented in court, immovables require special safeguards. The three conditions—defining boundaries, establishing possession through evidence, and making a demand—are designed to eliminate ambiguity and prevent fraudulent claims. We'll explore each condition and also examine a notable intra-Hanafi disagreement over the number of boundaries required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
Read the source passage carefully and list the three requirements the author states for a valid claim on immovable property.
Conditions: (1) defining boundaries, (2) stating possession in defendant's hand, (3) demanding the property.
2
Understand why boundaries are needed
The author explains that because an immovable cannot be brought to court, identification by pointing is impossible. Therefore, the plaintiff must describe the boundaries, including the names and lineages of adjoining owners, and according to Abu Hanifa, the grandfather's name for complete identification.
If the adjoining owner is well-known, mentioning his name alone suffices.
3
Recognize the possession proof rule
For immovables, the plaintiff's mere statement or the defendant's agreement that the property is in the defendant's hand is not enough. Possession must be established by evidence (bayyina) or the judge's knowledge. This is to prevent collusion.
For movables, the plaintiff's word suffices because possession is observable.
4
Note the demand requirement
The plaintiff must explicitly demand the property from the defendant. This eliminates possibilities such as the property being held as a pledge or detained for a price.
For movables, the demand must include the phrase 'without right'.
5
Consider the dispute with Imam Zufar
The text notes that if the plaintiff mentions only three boundaries, Abu Hanifa and the majority (including Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) accept it, while Imam Zufar requires all four. The majority view relies on the principle that the majority suffices and omission of one boundary does not change the claim.
The text says 'according to us' (عندنا), indicating the mufta bihi is three boundaries.

گا پس اگر مدعی نے تین حدود ذکر کیں تو ہمارے نزدیک ان پر اکتفاء کیا جائے گا۔ امام زفر کا اختلاف ہے اس لئے کہ اکثر حدود پائی گئیں۔ برخلاف اس کے جبکہ چوتھی حد بیان کرنے میں غلطی کی اس لئے کہ اس سے دعوی نہیں کیا جائے گا بلکہ عقار میں قبضہ ثابت نہیں ہوگا مگر گواہوں سے یا قاضی کو معلوم ہو یہی صحیح ہے تا کہ باہمی ساز باز کی تہمت کی نفی ہو سکے کیونکہ بہت ممکن ہے کہ عقار ان دونوں کے علاوہ کے قبضہ میں ہو علیہ کے قبضہ میں بطور رہن ہو یا اس کے قبضہ میں ثمن کی وجہ سے محبوس ہو اور مطالبہ سے یہ احتمال زائل ہو جاتا ہے اور یہیں سے مشائخ نے کہا کہ منقول میں واجب ہے کہ یہ کہے کہ مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ میں یہ چیز ناحق ہے اور گر مدعی ذمہ میں کوئی حق ہو تو مدعی ذکر کرے کہ وہ مدعی علیہ اس حق کا مطالبہ کرتا ہے اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی۔ اور یہ اس واسطے کہ صاحب ذمہ تو حاضر ہوا پس سوائے مطالبہ کے کچھ باقی نہ رہا لیکن بیان وصف کے ساتھ اس حق کی شناخت کرانا ضروری ہے کیونکہ وہ حق بیان وصف سے معلوم ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مدعی نے کسی غیر منقول چیز مثلا زمین یا مکان کا دعوی کیا تو اس دعوی کے صحیح ہونے کے لئے تین چیزیں ضروری ہیں۔
۱۔ مدعی ، اس شی مدعی بہ کے حدود بیان کرے یعنی یہ بیان کرے کہ مدعی یہ کی مشرقی جانب کا فلاں مالک ہے مغربی جانب کا فلاں ، شمالی جانب کا فلاں اور جنوبی جانب کا فلاں مالک ہے۔

The plaintiff should also state that the claimed thing is in the possession of the defendant. 3. And also state that he has demanded this claimed thing from the defendant. The proof of the first is that since transferring an immovable thing to court is impossible, identification by pointing is not possible. When it is not possible for the plaintiff to identify the claimed thing by pointing, then mentioning its boundaries becomes necessary, because immovable property is known in this way. Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Da'wa (Book of Lawsuit) in Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the procedural requirements for filing a lawsuit regarding immovable property ('aqar). The author begins by noting a general rule: a defendant must answer 'yes' or 'no' to the claim. For movables, the item must be presented in court; if destroyed or lost, the plaintiff must state its value and, according to Abu al-Layth, also its gender. Then the focus shifts to immovables. The core ruling is that for a claim on immovable property, three conditions must be met: (1) the plaintiff must define the property by mentioning its four boundaries, including the names and lineages of adjoining owners, and according to Abu Hanifa, the grandfather's name is necessary for full identification; (2) he must state that the property is in the defendant's possession; (3) he must state that he demands it from the defendant. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that since an immovable cannot be brought to court, identification by pointing is impossible, so boundaries must be used. For possession, the text warns against relying solely on the plaintiff's statement or the defendant's confirmation due to the risk of collusion; possession must be proven by witnesses or the judge's knowledge. The demand is necessary to eliminate possibilities like the property being a pledge or held for a price. The author also notes an intra-Hanafi disagreement with Imam Zufar: if the plaintiff mentions three boundaries (instead of four), Abu Hanifa and the majority accept it, but Zufar does not. The same requirement for boundaries applies in testimony as well. For movables, since possession is observable, the plaintiff's statement suffices, but he must explicitly say 'in his hand without right'. This passage is a detailed expansion of the matn of Al-Quduri, typical of later Hanafi commentary.

Key Terms
عقار ('aqar): Immovable property such as land or buildings; property that cannot be moved to court.
تحدید (tahdid): Defining the boundaries of immovable property by mentioning adjoining owners.
ید (yad): Possession or control over property; being in one's hand.
مطالبہ (mutalaba): Demand for the property; the plaintiff's explicit request for the property from the defendant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a plaintiff mentions only three boundaries instead of four?
A) The claim is invalid according to all Hanafi scholars.
B) The claim is valid according to Abu Hanifa and the majority, but invalid according to Imam Zufar.
C) The claim is valid only if the fourth boundary is unknown.
D) The claim is invalid because all four boundaries are required.

Key Takeaway
For a valid claim on immovable property, the plaintiff must define boundaries (at least three), prove possession through evidence or judicial knowledge, and explicitly demand the property.

Requirements for Describing Boundaries in Property Claims
Intra-Hanafi dispute on boundary description requirements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirements for describing boundaries in property claims and explain why mentioning three boundaries suffices, distinguishing omission from error.

Core Idea
In property claims, mentioning three boundaries is enough because the majority stands for the whole; omission is not error.

When claiming ownership of immovable property, the claimant must describe the property precisely to avoid confusion. The Hanafi school has detailed rules on what constitutes a sufficient description, including the names and lineage of the boundary owners. A key dispute within the school concerns whether omitting one of the four boundaries invalidates the claim or not. This lesson unpacks that dispute and the underlying principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the required elements for describing boundaries
From the text, list the elements: mention the city, the specific location within the city, the four boundaries, and the names (including grandfather) of the boundary owners.
The grandfather is required according to Abu Hanifa for full identification; well-known persons like Ibn Abi Layla are exceptions.
2
Understand the dispute: three boundaries vs. four
The text states that if three boundaries are mentioned correctly and the fourth is omitted, the Hanafi school (Imam Abu Hanifa and others except Imam Zufar) accepts the claim, while Imam Zufar rejects it.
Imam Zufar analogizes omission to error, which would invalidate the claim.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof: al-akthar ka al-kull
The Hanafi position relies on the principle that the majority holds the status of the whole. Since three boundaries constitute the majority, the ruling for four boundaries applies to three.
This principle is supported by an analogy from testimony: omitting the price in a testimonial is excused, but a wrong price invalidates.
4
Distinguish omission from error
The text explains that omission (tark) is different from error (ghalat): an omitted boundary remains in its place and the property can still be identified, whereas an erroneous boundary changes the subject matter.
Imam Zufar's qiyas is invalid because the two cases are fundamentally different.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a claimant who mentions three boundaries correctly and omits the fourth. According to the Hanafi school, his claim is valid. If he mentions two boundaries only, it is invalid.
The principle 'al-akthar ka al-kull' requires at least three, as two do not constitute a majority.

Book of Claims. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume ... He should mention the city in which the claimed property is located, then in the city the place where it is located, then the four boundaries of the claimed property. When mentioning the four boundaries, it is also necessary to mention the names and lineage of the owners of the boundaries. For example, he should say: 'The claimant, the owner of the eastern side is Khalid ibn Hamid ibn Majid.' Sahib al-Bada'i says: It is also necessary to mention the grandfather in the names and lineage of the boundary owners because according to Imam Abu Hanifa, identification is fully achieved by mentioning the grandfather. As has been learned elsewhere, and this is the correct statement. Sahib al-Hidayah said: If any of the boundary owners is well-known and famous, such as Ibn Abi Layla, Imam Muhammad, etc., then it will be sufficient to mention only his name, i.e., just his name without lineage. And if the claimant mentions only three of the four boundaries and does not mention the fourth, then according to us it is sufficient, and according to Imam Zufar mentioning only three boundaries is not sufficient. Imam Zufar's evidence is that he analogizes the case of omission to that of error; i.e., just as making a mistake in mentioning a boundary invalidates the claim, similarly in the case of omission the claim will be invalid. Our evidence is that in this case the majority of boundaries have been mentioned, and the majority holds the status of the whole, so the ruling of the whole is applied to the majority. From this it is also understood that mentioning only two boundaries will not be sufficient. However, if the claimant correctly mentions three boundaries but mentions the fourth incorrectly, then this claim will be invalid because due to the error in mentioning the boundary of the claimed property, the claimed property has become different, so the claim will not be valid. In the case of omitting the fourth boundary, this does not apply because it remains in its place even if not mentioned. Just as if two witnesses testify to a sale and receipt of the price but omit mentioning the price, their testimony is valid; but if they make a mistake in mentioning the price, their testimony is not valid. After this distinction between omission and error, Imam Zufar's analogy of omission to error is also not valid.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the required description of boundaries in a claim for immovable property. The general rule: the claimant must identify the property by mentioning all four boundaries and the names of their owners, including their lineage up to the grandfather (following Imam Abu Hanifa's view that full identification requires three names). For well-known persons like Ibn Abi Layla or Imam Muhammad, just the name suffices. The core dispute: if three out of four boundaries are mentioned without the fourth, the Hanafi position (followed by Abu Hanifa and his students except Imam Zufar) accepts it as sufficient, based on the principle 'the majority is treated as the whole' (al-akthar ka al-kull). Imam Zufar rejects this, analogizing omission (tark) to error (ghalat), where an erroneous boundary invalidates the claim. The Hanafi response distinguishes omission from error: in omission, the unmentioned boundary remains in its place and does not misidentify the property; in error, the claim is about a different thing. An example is given from testimony: omitting the price in a testimonial about sale is excused, but a wrong price invalidates the testimony. Therefore, three boundaries suffice, but two do not.

Key Terms
حدود (hudūd): The four boundaries (directions) of a piece of immovable property that must be described in a claim
ترک (tark): Omitting to mention one of the required elements (e.g., a boundary) in the claim
غلطی (ghalaṭ): Mistake in describing a boundary, such as mentioning the wrong name or direction
اکثر (akthar): The majority; here, three out of four boundaries

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a claimant mentions three boundaries correctly but omits the fourth, what is the ruling?
A) The claim is invalid because all four boundaries must be mentioned
B) The claim is valid because the majority stands for the whole
C) The claim is valid only if the fourth boundary is unknown to the claimant
D) The claim is invalid if the fourth boundary is known but omitted

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi property claims, mentioning three out of four boundaries suffices because the majority takes the ruling of the whole, and omission does not equate to error.

Proving Possession in Immovable Property Claims Through Witnesses
States requirement of witness testimony for immovable property possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi fiqh requires witness testimony to prove the defendant's possession in immovable property claims and distinguish the rule for movable property.

Core Idea
Witness testimony for immovable property possession prevents collusion between claimant and defendant.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a key procedural rule in property claims: how to prove that the defendant possesses the claimed immovable property. It explains why the court cannot rely solely on the claimant's statement and defendant's acknowledgment, and why third-party testimony is required. Understanding this rule illustrates the Hanafi commitment to preventing fraud in property litigation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what legal act is being ruled upon. Here, it is proving the defendant's possession in a claim for immovable property. The ruling is that witness testimony (bayyinah) is required; mere assertion and acknowledgment are insufficient.
This is a procedural condition for the court to accept the claim.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the possibility of collusion (tuhma) between the claimant and defendant. They might falsely agree that the defendant possesses the property to get a judgment in the claimant's favor and then share the property.
The dalil is rational (aqlī), based on blocking the means to evil (sadd al-dharā'i‘).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The risk of collusion necessitates stronger evidence to prevent injustice. Witness testimony from disinterested third parties eliminates this risk because they have no motive to lie.
The reasoning is that the defendant's acknowledgment alone is tainted by the potential for conspiracy.
4
Note the exception for movable property
For movable property (manqūl), witness testimony is not required because possession is apparent (zāhir) and serves as evidence of ownership. The risk of collusion is lower since possession is observable.
This contrast highlights the rationale: the rule is driven by the nature of the property and the ease of verifying possession.

صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جس طرح دعوی میں حدود کا بیان کرنا شرط ہے اسی طرح گواہی میں بھی حدود کا بیان کرنا شرط ہوگا یعنی جو لوگ اس دعوئی پر گواہ ہوں گے وہ بھی حدود بیان کریں گے دوسری چیز کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مدعی علیہ اس وقت ختم قرار پائے گا جبکہ شی مدعی به اس کے قبضہ میں ہو۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں عقار (غیر منقول چیز ) میں مدعی کے بیان کرنے اور مدعی علیہ کی تصدیق کرنے پر کہ یہ عقار میرے قبضہ میں اکتفاء نہیں کیا جائے گا یعنی اگر عقار کا دعویٰ کیا اور ذکر کیا کہ عقار مذکور مدنی علیہ کے قبضہ میں ہے اور مدعی علیہ نے اس امر کا اقرار کر لیا کہ جس عقار پر دعویٰ ہے وہ میرے قبضہ میں ہے تو یہ کافی نہ ہوگا بلکہ بینہ سے مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ کو ثابت کرنا ضروری ہوگا یعنی گواہ اس بات پر گواہی دیں گے کہ ہم نے مذکورہ عقار کو اس مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ میں دیکھا ہے حتی کہ اگر گواہوں نے کہا کہ ہم نے سنا ہے کہ عقار مذکور مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ میں ہے تو یہ گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی۔ یا قاضی کو ذاتی طور پر معلوم ہو کہ عقار مذکور مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ میں ہے دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ مدعی کے یہ بیان کرنے میں کہ عقار ندکور مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ میں ہے اور مدعی علیہ کے اقرار کرنے میں تہمت کا امکان ہے اس طور پر کہ عقار مذکور کو ان دونوں کے علاوہ کسی تیسرے آدمی کے قبضہ میں ہو۔ اور ان دونوں نے اس زمین کو ہتھیانے کے لئے اس پر اتفاق کر لیا کہ مدعی یہ بیان کریگا کہ عقار مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ میں ہے اور مدعی علیہ اس کی تصدیق کرے گا اور پھر قاضی مدعی کے لئے قبضہ کا فیصلہ کر دے گا پھر دونوں بانٹ کر کھائیں گے پس تہمت کے اس امکان کو دور کرنے کے لئے کہا گیا کہ صرف مدعی کا بیان کرنا اور مدعی علیہ کا اس کی تصدیق کرنا کافی نہ ہوگا بلکہ مدعلی علیہ کے قبضہ کو گواہوں کے ذریعہ ثابت کرنا ضروری ہوگا اس کے برخلاف اگر مدنی بہ مال منقول ہو تو اس پر مدعلی علیہ کے قبضہ کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے بینہ کا پیش کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے کیونکہ مال معقول میں قبضہ شاہد ہوتا ہے اور قبضہ دلیل ملکیت ہے لہذا اس صورت میں بغیر بینہ کے مدعی علیہ کا قبضہ ثابت ہو جائے گا اور دعوی صحیح ہو جائے گا۔
Sahib al-Hidayah says: Just as it is a condition to mention boundaries in the claim, similarly it will be a condition to mention boundaries in the testimony i.e., those who testify to this claim will also mention boundaries. The proof of another matter is that the defendant will be considered to have surrendered only when the claimed property is in his possession. Sahib al-Hidayah says: In the case of immovable property ('aqar), it will not be sufficient for the claimant to merely state and the defendant to confirm that this property is in my possession. That is, if a claim is made for immovable property and it is mentioned that the said property is in the defendant's possession, and the defendant acknowledges that the property claimed is in his possession, this will not be sufficient. Rather, it is necessary to prove the defendant's possession through evidence (bayyinah), i.e., witnesses will testify that they have seen the said property in the possession of this defendant. Even if the witnesses say that they have heard that the said property is in the defendant's possession, this testimony will not be accepted. Or the judge personally knows that the said property is in the defendant's possession. The proof of this is that there is a possibility of collusion in the claimant's statement that the said property is in the defendant's possession and the defendant's acknowledgment, in the manner that the said property may be in the possession of a third person other than these two, and they have agreed to usurp this land by having the claimant state that the property is in the defendant's possession and the defendant confirm it, then the judge will decide possession in favor of the claimant, and they will share and consume it. So to eliminate the possibility of collusion, it was said that only the claimant's statement and the defendant's confirmation will not suffice; rather, it is necessary to prove the defendant's possession through witnesses. In contrast, if the claimed property is movable property, then it is not necessary to present evidence to prove the defendant's possession, because in movable property, possession is apparent (zahir) and possession is evidence of ownership. Therefore, in this case, without evidence, the defendant's possession will be established and the claim will be valid.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage establishes two rules. First, the requirement of boundary description extends to witnesses: those testifying must also mention boundaries. Second, for immovable property, mere assertion by the claimant and acknowledgment by the defendant are insufficient to prove that the property is in the defendant's possession; witnesses must testify to having seen it in the defendant's possession. The reason is the possibility of collusion (tuhma): the claimant and defendant might conspire to falsely claim that the property is in the defendant's possession, obtain a judgment in the claimant's favor, and then divide the property. Testimony by third parties prevents this. For movable property, this requirement is waived because possession of movables is inherently apparent (zahir) and serves as evidence of ownership. Thus, for movables, the defendant's possession is accepted without witness proof.

Key Terms
عقار ('aqār): Immovable property (land, buildings)
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence, specifically witness testimony in court
تہمت (tuhma): Suspicion or possibility of collusion or fraud between the claimant and defendant

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is witness testimony required to prove the defendant's possession in claims for immovable property but not for movable property?
A) Because movable property is more valuable
B) Because the possibility of collusion is higher in immovable property claims
C) Because movable property is always in the defendant's possession
D) Because the claimant must prove ownership for immovable property

Key Takeaway
For immovable property, witness testimony is required to prove the defendant's possession due to the risk of collusion; for movable property, possession is apparent and no witnesses are needed.

Requirement of Demand in Claims
Explains the necessity of demanding property in claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two reasons why demanding the property is wajib in a claim and apply the rule that for movables the phrase 'bilā ḥaqq' is required.

Core Idea
Claimant must demand the property to exclude lawful possession (e.g., mortgage) or the claim fails.

In Hanafi fiqh, simply asserting ownership is not enough to make a claim valid. The claimant must also demand the property from the defendant. This lesson explores why this demand (mutalaba) is necessary and how it eliminates the presumption that the property might be lawfully held, such as under a mortgage or as security for an unpaid price. For movable property, an even stricter requirement applies: the claimant must explicitly say the property is held 'unjustly' (bilā ḥaqq).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the claimant's demand (mutalaba) for the claimed property. The act is ruled wajib (obligatory) for the claim to be valid.
The requirement applies to both immovable and movable property, but with an additional condition for movables.
2
Locate the two proofs (adillah)
The text gives two proofs: (1) demanding the property is the claimant's right, so exercising a right is necessary; (2) to eliminate the possibility that the property is lawfully held (e.g., mortgaged or held for price).
These are rational proofs (dalil aqli) rather than revealed texts.
3
Trace the rationale of proof 2
If the defendant's possession could be lawful (e.g., mortgagee), then the claim would not be valid because the defendant has a right to possess. By demanding the property, the claimant shows he does not acknowledge any lawful basis, thus removing the possibility.
This is a matter of negating a probabilistic excuse for the defendant.
4
Apply the additional condition for movables
For movable property, the demand must include the phrase 'bilā ḥaqq' (without right/unjustly). This explicitly denies any lawful cause like mortgage or detention for price.
The Mashayikh derived this because movables are often held lawfully in such transactions.
5
Determine the legal effect
If the claimant demands without the phrase for movables, the claim may be invalid or the possibility of lawful possession remains. Including 'bilā ḥaqq' ensures the claim is legally sound.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور تیسری چیز کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مدعی یہ مدعی کا حق ہے بہزاد ٹی مالیہ سے اس کا مطالبہ بھی مدعی کاحق ہوگا اور جب مطالبہ حق کا ہے تو مدعی کیلئے مطالبہ کرنا یعنی مدعی بہ کو طلب کرنا بھی ضروری ہوگا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہاں یہ احتمال موجود ہے کہ مدعی نے مدعی علیہ سے قرضہ لے کر یہ عقار اس کے پاس بطور رہن رکھدی ہو۔ یا مدعی نے اس سے اس عقار کو خریدا ہو لیکن شن نہ ادا کرنے کی وجہ سے مدعلی علیہ نے اس کو روک لیا ہو تو یہ قبضہ دعوی صحیح ہونے کی دلیل نہ ہوگا لیکن جب مدعی نے اس عقار کا مطالبہ کیا اور مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ سے اس کو نکالنے کا ارادہ کیا تو یہ احتمال زائل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ جو چیز مرہون یا شمن میں محبوس ہو تو وہ قابض کے قبضہ سے نہیں نکالی جاتی ہے اور اس کا اس طرح مطالبہ نہیں کیا جاتا ہے پس جب مدعی نے مطالبہ کیا تو اس عقار کے مرہون یا محبوس ہونے کا احتمال نہ رہا بہر حال اس احتمال کو رد کرنے کے لئے مطالبہ کرنا ضروری ہے۔ یہیں سے مشائخ نے یہ بات کہی کہ اگر دعوی بھی منقول میں ہوتو مودی کا یہ کہنا ضروری ہوگا کہ بیٹی مدعی علیہ کے قبضہ میں ناحق طور پر اسلئے کہ ناحق کہنے کے بعد اس شی کے مرہون یا محبوس با شمن ہونے کا احتمال نہیں رہے گا کیونکہ شی ، مرهون پر مرتین کا قبضہ اورشی محبوس پر بالع کا قبضہ بجا اور حق ہوتا ہے۔
And the proof of the third matter is that the claimed property is the claimant's right; demanding it from the defendant is also the claimant's right. And when the demand is a right, it becomes necessary for the claimant to make the demand, i.e., to request the claimed property. The second proof is that there exists a possibility that the claimant took a loan from the defendant and placed this property as a mortgage with him, or that the claimant purchased this property from him but due to non-payment of the price the defendant has detained it. So this possession would not be proof that the claim is valid. But when the claimant demands this property and intends to remove it from the defendant's possession, this possibility is eliminated, because anything that is mortgaged or held as security for the price is not taken out of the possessor's possession and is not demanded in this manner. So when the claimant makes the demand, there remains no possibility that this property is mortgaged or held as security. Nevertheless, to rebut this possibility, making the demand is obligatory. From here, the Mashayikh said: If the claim is for movable property, it will be necessary for the claimant to say that the property is in the defendant's possession unjustly (bilā ḥaqq), because after saying 'unjustly', there will remain no possibility of the property being mortgaged or held as security for the price, because the possession of a mortgagee over a mortgaged property and the possession of a seller over property held for the price is proper and right.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage discusses the third condition for a valid claim: the claimant must demand (mutalaba) the property from the defendant. The reasons given are: (1) it is the claimant's right to demand his property, and (2) to eliminate the possibility that the property is in the defendant's possession lawfully, such as being mortgaged for a debt or held as security for an unpaid price. If it were lawfully held, the mere assertion of a claim would not suffice to prove it is wrongfully possessed. By demanding the property, the claimant indicates that he is not acknowledging any lawful right of the defendant. For movable property, the demand must explicitly include the word 'bilā ḥaqq' (without right), because possession of movables could be lawful (e.g., mortgagee's possession). Stating 'unjustly' removes any suggestion of lawful cause. This ruling is derived from the Mashāyikh (later Hanafi authorities).

Key Terms
مطالبہ (muṭālaba): The act of the claimant demanding the property from the defendant, a required element in a claim
ناحق (bi-lā ḥaqq): Without right; unjustly; used in the demand for movable property to exclude lawful causes of possession
رہن (rahn): Mortgage; a contract where property is held as security for a debt

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why must the claimant demand the property explicitly, including the phrase 'bilā ḥaqq' for movable property?
A) To prove the defendant's bad character
B) To eliminate the possibility that the property is lawfully held as mortgage or security
C) To establish the value of the property
D) To fulfill a procedural formality only

Key Takeaway
A claim in Hanafi law requires the claimant to demand the property to negate lawful possession; for movables, the demand must include 'bilā ḥaqq'.
